Its a clipper and its not going to be whisper quiet.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I am aware that these devices are designed to be disposable and after about a year or so I found the blades to get a little dull. My barber charges 10 bucks for lineups and trims in between full blown haircuts so this allows me to skip the weekly trips to the barbershop. It makes quick work of even the thickest beards, and you may actually need to be careful when shaving around delicate areas.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Although the battery choice is excellent, and the cutters are solid, the flaws in this device lie with the accessories.  This is not due to lack of attachments, as there are nearly a dozen included.  There actually are too many attachments, which overcomplicate using the device and create far too many small parts that could be lost.  While some of the attachments are quite useful, some are flimsy and near useless, such as the eyebrow trimmer.  The plethora of attachments should have been combined into a small handful of adjustable ones instead.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Although lacking an adjustable trimmer attachment, this device is still an excellent trimmer, with a rock solid motor and great battery.  While I can&#x27;t give it five stars, it is definitely a purchase worth considering.</li>

    <li> I read a lot of the reviews and that helped me make my decision. I&#x27;ve had this trimmer a couple of months now, and really love it. I&#x27;ll start with the points I did NOT find easily in other reviews    Yes, it does a great job trimming the edges of your mustache above the lip, etc. I&#x27;ve had all-in-one beard groomers where the trimming attachment did not cut well. Not so with this one. The first time I used it I was instantly showing a lot more lip than I had planned on. In other words, it trims mustaches better than anything I have used before.    The other point I was unclear about in other reviews was the usefulness of the nose/ear trimmer attachment. I have owned 2 or 3 of those battery powered rotating types before, and always found them so-so. This trimmer attachment does a much better job than those, and is faster. Just stick it in your ear or nose and you&#x27;re done in 2 seconds, whereas the rotary types make you keep doing it for a while before it seems like you&#x27;re done. The noise level is not a problem at all for me - it&#x27;s noisy but not objectionable in your ear, about the same or less noise level as my rotary trimmer.    For beard trimming (I have a goatee that I keep fairly short), it works well but is slightly less convenient than the all-in-one beard groomers I have owned. You have to switch attachments, which is frankly very easy, though not as easy as just dialing in a 3 or 4 on one of those beard groomers. And the attachments are a bit of a pain because you have to either pick, for instance, a 2 or 3 beard trimmer, or else use the 6-position trimmer attachment. That 6-position trimmer attachment is what I use, and it&#x27;s fine, though adjusting it&#x27;s height requires a little more effort than it should.    Battery life is outstanding, and what puts it above everything else. It lasted 2 months of frequent use on its first charge, and I expect it to last for years. Other beard groomers I have owned (both Panasonic) died after a couple of years and had to be plugged in.    The attachments in general are a bit of a pain, as everyone else mentions. However, putting them on and off is really easy - not as complicated (at least to me) as others have mentioned. I keep them all in the tray on my countertop and it works fairly well. The tray gets really crowded, so I&#x27;ve take some of the attachments I&#x27;m never going to use and put them in a drawer. It is nice to have your oil and brush right there whenever you need them - otherwise I would not clean and oil it as often as I should:)    For haircutting, I agree with everyone else. This thing is really narrow, even with the wider cutting head attached. It&#x27;s about half the width of my corded Wahl trimmer, which is what I&#x27;ve been using to cut my hair (and does a great job). Also, the attachments are not long enough for my hair, which normally takes a 4 and a 5 attachment. Not sure if you can buy longer attachments for it or not. I think the best solution is just to spend another 30 bucks on the corded Wahl unit like I did. It&#x27;s a beast, seems to actually dim the lights when you turn it on (semi-kidding here but you get the idea).    For all around trimming, meaning sideburns and hairline at back of neck, it&#x27;s super. The normal attachment does a great job of shaping your hair and cuts super sharp.    In sum - it&#x27;s outstanding for moustache/ear/nose trimming as well as shaping your beard or hair at the edges. Don&#x27;t bother thinking it&#x27;s going to be very good for actually cutting your hair.</li>

    <li> (This is an updated review)  My previous comment explained the annoyance of Wahl&#x27;s warranty service. A Wahl representative responded to my original amazon comment stating that my comment (that is, my quotation of product warranty) does not accurately reflect Wahl&#x27;s service. And indeed he&#x27;s right; warranty service worked as it should. So, when in doubt, contact someone, and don&#x27;t follow the written instruction unless you have to.    It&#x27;d be nice if the warranty description that comes with the product was accurate, but given that the instruction booklet that comes with the trimmer is rather generic (describes features of other models as well), I&#x27;m guessing they haven&#x27;t updated that text in a long time. I use an electric shaver (Braun 7680) for day-to-day and the Wahl every few days for the goatee. The high-torque means a fast and accurate trim (lesser trimmers you have to keep running over the same area over and over) and the LiOn means I don&#x27;t have to worry if I&#x27;ve got enough charge left to get a good trim.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I have to admit that I really appreciate the shaver/blade/accessories tray that comes with this Wahl. I was always losing bit and pieces from other trimmers, but with this tray I can keep everything together.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Powerful, long lasting charge, lots of clipping/trimming/detailing options and a tray to keep all the parts together...This is a nice set, I certainly recommend it.with this Wahl.     <li> We have owned several of this type of trimmer over the years, and this one falls somewhere in the middle of the pack. While we liked that Wahl is still a family-owned company, and the shaver was made in the US, the quality feels a little cheap for the price. Lightweight plastic components don&#x27;t say \\&quot;long-lasting quality\\&quot; to me. The method of attachment is awkward, with attachments held on by stiff plastic clips which I don&#x27;t believe will last particularly long if used often. It takes quite a bit of force to snap them on; making me feel pretty sure they will snap off at some point before I&#x27;m ready to be done using this product. The shaver does, however, hold a charge remarkably well, which is its main selling point. It comes with every conceivable attachment, making it versatile for any use you can think of. And it does what it claims to do: it trims and shaves hair admirably. The motor seems to have significantly more power than its predecessor at our house.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Bottom line: it works and works well, but I don&#x27;t see it having the durability to hold up to long term use. Higher quality materials would have made this a 5 star product.</li>
    <li> The standard against which a multiple use product like this is to be measured is NOT whether it is the best performing product at each task, but rather whether it performs well enough to replace two or more items in your bathroom or more importantly in your carry on luggage.  As a habitually clean-shaven man, I might seem a poor choice to review such a product, but a fortuitously timed job layoff has allowed me to grow a beard in order to fully test the device.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;BATTERY: This is the major selling point; I fully charged it when I received it and have been using it off and on over the last two months ON THE VERY FIRST CHARGE, and it is still going strong!  There is no other rechargeable battery technology I&#x27;m aware of that could even approach, much less match that performance.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;SHAVER HEAD: As a blade shaver whose weapon of choice is the [[ASIN:B000XVXK12 Gillette Fusion Power Phenom Razor]], I have always believed that electric razors are for men who don&#x27;t really insist on a close shave (or less facetiously for men whose lifestyle requires shaving on-the-go).  Nothing about the performance of this trimmer&#x27;s shaver head has changed my mind, and for shaving the entire face it is clearly inferior to the [[ASIN:B001FA1F8K Braun Series 1 1-150 Men&#x27;s Shaver]] I have also been testing.  However, in fairness, it was never really intended for this purpose.  No man in his right mind would choose such a product unless he was planning to at least experiment with facial hair, and for the purpose of shaving those parts of your face not covered by your beard or mustache, it is quite adequate.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;DETAIL HEAD: For delicate work, like separating that unibrow into two separate eyebrows, the detail head works fine, though perhaps because of the small size of its face plate, it becomes uncomfortably warm during sustained use.  However, as a nose hair or ear hair trimmer, it is clearly inferior to any with rotary heads.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;TRIMMER HEAD: The main trimmer head comes with far too many attachments IMHO, and I don&#x27;t say that just because in mine all of the plastic attachments displayed in the box window were duplicated inside.  Unless you are planning a career as a traveling beard stylist, a six-position trimmer guide and 3 fixed-length attachment combs is probably going to be more than you will ever need.  However, experimentation will be required in order to narrow down your choices.  The adjustable trimmer guide provides more choices without switching attachments, but it is susceptible to slipping under pressure, resulting in a closer trim than you intended.  For body hair trimming, this device is clearly inferior to the [[ASIN:B000EG8HLE Philips Norelco BG2020 Bodygroom Shaver]], [[ASIN:B000TFNH1U Philips Norelco Body Groomer Limited Edition BG2022]], and probably to the [[ASIN:B001E0C9LI Philips Norelco BG2030 Professional BodyGrooming System]] as well, in everything except battery, but unless you are a performer in the adult film industry, it will probably do an adequate job, especially if you have someone who can assist you with the underbrush thinning.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Note: Unless you plan on regularly maintaining yourself in that condition, it is not advisable to shave yourself too closely between the waist and the knees.  Two words -- \\&quot;razor stubble\\&quot; -- in close contact with your most tender areas should be explanation enough.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;T-BLADE HEAD:  Unless you develop the habit of using it to trim your beard or are still maintaining that boot camp &#x27;doo, this will probably be the least useful blade unless you have a partner with some haircutting skills because while any idiot can eventually learn to trim his own beard, cutting your own hair in a manner you&#x27;d be willing to display in public is probably going to be beyond your abilities.  However, Wahl made its name in hair clippers and could hardly be expected to leave one out of an all-in-one trimmer.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Defects?  The lack of a carrying case is particularly felt with such a large number of attachments, and a vacuum feature to capture hair clippings would be a nice-to-have. In addition the handle has the ergonomics of a flashlight, but these are minor points.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In summation for a bearded or mustachioed man on the go this device CAN adequately replace everything it claims to replace with the exception of a nose hair trimmer.vacuum feature to capture hair clippings would be a nice-to-have. In addition the handle has the ergonomics of a flashlight, but these are minor points.    In summation for a bearded or mustachioed man on the go this device CAN adequately replace everything it claims to replace with the exception of a nose hair trimmer.</li>

    <li> Contrary to some reviews here, you cannot use it when it&#x27;s not charged (but plugged-in). It only works after charging, and plugging it in while using it does not bypass the battery (so that it can be used when the battery is dead).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;For this reason, it gets 3/5.</li>

    <li> I replaced a basic rechargeable Wahl trimmer that had to be over 15 yr&#x27;s old (battery finally went belly up), &amp; will stop using a Braun trimmer that&#x27;s difficult to use. The latter doesn&#x27;t hold a charge for very long anymore, &amp; I got tired of skin scratches as the cutting guard teeth were too sharp.    I bought the Wahl Lithium Ion trimmer primarily for sideburn, neck, &amp; \\&quot;nether\\&quot; region trimming purposes, as well as for the Lithium Ion battery. I too draw weary of the old cadmium rechargeable battery shortcomings (short charge durations + memory problems).     I used the trim &amp; clip attachments for sideburn, neckline (front &amp; back), &amp; groin trimming. The latter for me has become habit for 20+ yr&#x27;s as I&#x27;m a former long distance cyclist, &amp; you learn quickly that that area is better off smooth for cycling purposes. Fortunately, many women love it also. Both attachments afforded me a very clean, close to the skin trim with no abrasion from the cutting guard teeth. Just as important, the teeth are close together &amp; I experienced no grabbing of skin or hair.    The foil shave attachment worked as well &amp; no better than other foil shavers I&#x27;ve used. I currently own a Braun rechargeable foil shaver, &amp; neither provides me a skin smooth shave. Given my experience, I don&#x27;t expect skin smooth shaves from a foil shaver. That&#x27;s why I use a blade for all of my shaving - to achieve the actual skin smooth results.    I also used the detail attachment on my ears &amp; nose. I found it no more effective than a real round headed ear/nose trimmer. Given the cutting edge &amp; angle it provides, I found it more difficult to use on my ears &amp; nose. So for the purpose of trimming ear &amp; nose hairs, I will continue to use my round headed ear &amp; nose hair trimmer (from Sharper Image - Turbo Groomer 5.0).     At this time I have no reason to test all of the guide combs for moustache &amp; beard trimming purposes as I no longer have either at this time. Having used such trimmer combs in the past, I see no reason why they won&#x27;t work well as they&#x27;re comparable in design as anything else I&#x27;ve ever used.    Some reviewers have noted that the trimmer is loud &amp; bothersome. I guess it depends on what you&#x27;re used to, but in my experience, it&#x27;s no louder than anything I&#x27;ve ever used, &amp; quiter than some. Some have also pointed out that hairs stick to the silicone rubber grip. Personally, I find that a mute point, as it&#x27;s easy to wipe them off by hand or with a towel. I wouldn&#x27;t base my purchasing decision on such a finding.    Bottom line is that it&#x27;s light weight &amp; easy to use. The battery provides more power than cadmium rechargeable batteries, &amp; having experienced Lithium Ion batteries in other products I own, I look forward to no longer wondering whether or not the battery will be there for me when I need it if I&#x27;ve not kept it plugged into the charger. The trimmer attachments provide a clean &amp; close trim. All in all, this trimmer is worth the $40.</li>
    <li> I don&#x27;t know why it is so difficult to find a good trimmer/groomer these days.  I purchased a \\&quot;cheapy\\&quot; in 2001 that lasted for 9 years and worked great (I forget the brand). My previous trimmer allowed the plug to be attached to the base so that the trimmer detached from the plug when lifting it, which I prefer.  - The 6-Position Guide is worthless if you want to use \\&quot;position 1\\&quot; setting (the setting that gives you the closest trim).  Every time I use that setting, I end up with bald patches along the trim line, and end up having to shave the entire area down/off to match. As I write this review, the Philips Norelco Qg3280/41 is on sale for 32 dol. so I&#x27;m going to give that a try and hope that I can end my hunt for a trimmer I can be satisfied with for the next several years.</li>

    <li> First off... People, be aware of \\&quot;Vine Program\\&quot; reviewers.     <li> Worked well for 10-months of very light duty trimming a goatee and sideburns and being kept clean and oiled up.  Today it failed to turn on after being plugged to charge.  Took the head off and inspected inside, very clean and the unit looks brand spanking new.  Wahl doesn&#x27;t have good customer service or warranty return service and their web site support is a joke.  So it is up to me to deal with the repair.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I tested the charger and it is producing a steady 4.30 V.  I disassembled the unit by pulling back the rubber cover down and splitting the plastic case open to expose the motor, battery and electronics.  There was corrosion and a layer of green on the integrated circuit leads due to ambient moisture in the bathroom.  Cleaned it off with vinegar and distilled water and checked the leads and the unit worked again.  The internal battery is an industrial a 3.7V 750 mAh 2.3 wh AA Lithium Ion and it was 3.95 V showing a full charge.  I will re-solder the weakened and corroded leads and put a waterproof layer of conformal coating on all the exposed leads and chips.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I suspect that Wahl knows about ambient moisture damaging and destroying the products and they refuse to cover the electronics with moisture resistant conformal coating used as an inexpensive and standard way in the electronics industry to ensure a steady stream of failures and re-purchases by customers.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My advice is open the unit up and waterproof the electronics by covering the leads and chips with a liquid or spray-on conformal coating.  If you&#x27;re not mechanical enough to do that, I suggest go buy another product and hope for the best.</li>

    <li> Pros:&lt;br /&gt;Solid-feeling trimmer&lt;br /&gt;Well-constructed blades&lt;br /&gt;Wide array of attachments&lt;br /&gt;Powerful motor&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Cons:&lt;br /&gt;ill-conceived base&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The WAHL Lithium-Ion All in One Trimmer is a reasonably good all-in-one trimmer. It has quite a strong motor that has no trouble going through very coarse facial hair. Its incredibly long battery life allows it to be taken on a week-long trip without any worry of losing performance. If a longer stint away from home is required, its small wall-wart DC adapter would fit inside of a dopp kit without any trouble.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;All of the blades included seem very well-constructed. They have very fine teeth that move smoothly. Unlike other inexpensive groomers, these blades are meant to be maintained (a good thing, in my opinion), and come with a small bottle of lubricating oil. Unfortunately, only two of the four blade attachments are truly useful.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The standard trimming blade with its four guide attachments handles the majority of trimming needs. It handles beards, sideburns, and *other* areas with comfortable ease. For closer shaves, the dual-foil blade handles the rest with very little irritation. I have very coarse facial hair that usually has to be taken off with a Mach 3 or better blade. The foil shaver (and great torque from the motor) managed to get through nearly all of the facial hair except for a few sensitive neck areas that weren&#x27;t used to an electric trimmer.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The other two blades, the hair trimmer and ear/nose trimmer, saw little use. The nose trimmer is much too large to fit comfortably in a nostril, and - though it has seven guide attachments in total -- there are no guide attachments for use on eyebrows (only a hand-held comb, which is easy to move). I usually leave the hair trimming to a barber, so I don&#x27;t foresee much use of the hair trimmer.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The only truly bad part of the trimmer is the accessory base. It is much larger than the trimmer itself, yet doesn&#x27;t hold the attachments well. They just sit loosely in the recessed areas, and are easily knocked out when the flimsy base gets knocked around.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This is the best trimmer I&#x27;ve used in this price range. I own the Remmington PG-350 (listed on the WAHL All-in-One box as the \\&quot;competition\\&quot;) and the WAHL 5570 and this is a better trimmer than both in terms of power and versatility.s, and are easily knocked out when the flimsy base gets knocked around.     <li> [3 week Update: I omitted this before, but, I bought this unit primarily to shave my head. (I keep my pate at about \\&quot;stubble level\\&quot; because I prefer that over complete smoothness.) So, I decided to try the Wahl Li-Ion Trimmer as a replacement of my previous, 3 year-old wahl trimmer/shaver, which was beginning to have charging &amp; power issues. And I have to say that, -for this specific purpose- the Wahl Li-Ion doesn&#x27;t quite \\&quot;cut\\&quot; it. In fact, despite offering a more consistent beard trimming experience, it actually takes more passes over my head to get the hair down to that afore-mentioned stubble. (Go figure.) Apart from this, the rest of my review remains pretty much in tact...]&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;About shipping/handling: I received the unit in only 3 days (ordered Sun.; arrived Wed.) despite my choosing the cheapest (read: \\&quot;free\\&quot;) shipping option. Kudos to Amazon for that! (I&#x27;m sure it doesn&#x27;t hurt that I live in Los Angeles.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;About the unit: Seems like a good, solid buy. Tested all the service attachments (blades &amp; dual-screen); 3 of the 4 seemed to work as well as any of the 5 or 6 shavers I&#x27;ve had in my adult life (though the dual-screen seems a skosh narrow for its intended purpose). The one attachment that seemed the least useful is the nose-hair trimmer. It just didn&#x27;t seem functional enough to warrant inclusion in the kit (though I think I understand why it was, given the niche for which this unit was designed).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Some have mentioned a qualm with the rubberized handle, noting that hairs seem to \\&quot;eagerly\\&quot; cling to it. Well ...duh. But I see it as more useful than annoying, since the sport of shaving can often involve slippage from the hand! Ergo: rubber is good! (c: (Here, I&#x27;ll also note that on the front of my unit - where the rubber meets the plastic - the upper edge of the rubber doesn&#x27;t perfectly align with the bottom edge of the plastic. A VERY minor flaw which would be a ridiculous reason to return it, but, it is what it is.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;\\&quot;Vibration\\&quot; issues have also been noted by some as problematic. Here, I wonder about the experience of most folks - as, a good, strong unit is bound to feel &amp; sound like it - especially at this price point! It wasn&#x27;t a concern for me at all, and so far has only reinforced the initial impression I have of, well ...a \\&quot;good, strong unit.\\&quot;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Now for a word of pure praise: Kudos to Wahl for their quickly interchangeable head system. Wowie-zowie but is that ever useful. Once I got the hang of it, those suckers went on &amp; off with panache! (It certainly raises the \\&quot;useful\\&quot; quotient by more than a bit!) I sure hope this feature keeps working for years to come. If so, then, it&#x27;ll definitely be a winning feature, in my book.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The one *potentially* serious concern I have about its design is the Li-Ion battery. I say &#x27;potentially&#x27; because, for the most part, I think the battery is a strength(!) I mean, come on ...a full shave after only a quick, 3-minute charge?! Seriously, that&#x27;s a real benefit, folks. I have yet to test it myself, but, am thinking I may need to, given the fact that (and here&#x27;s my \\&quot;concern\\&quot;) a company representative admitted that the battery&#x27;s \\&quot;smart-chip\\&quot; -tasked with overcharge prevention- may also prevent any charge at all if the unit is left plugged in for more than 3 hours. (Note to self: unplug after 3 hours!) A tad annoying, but, problem easily solved, nevertheless.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;So, four stars (or maybe 3.75), due to the few (relatively) minor design flaws detailed above. Ultimately, though, I see this unit as a pretty decent deal - especially given the $32 price (sans shipping).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;PS: the plastic stand isn&#x27;t quite as shabby as others have made it out to be. I&#x27;ve found it to be of pretty standard grade. Though, admittedly, it doesn&#x27;t do the best job of housing all the accessories.some as problematic.     <li> Like the title says, I&#x27;m on my second one of these, as the old one finally gave out (battery issue).  I got about four years use out of the old one, it had a Ni-MH battery in it, so I guess it&#x27;s really not a huge surprise.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;What I like about this new one:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;+ Same design as the older model, but it has a newly redesigned holding tray which will now hold all of the attachments (though the product packaging displays the old one).  The older designed tray never would hold them all, so some wound up sitting in a drawer.  As a bonus, now that I have this newer model I have backup attachments since WAHL stayed with the same design *nice*.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;+ New Li-ion battery -- it seems like it&#x27;s more powerful than the older version, though both work well.  The new battery requires less charging time, and seems like it lasts longer.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;+ Plenty of attachments -- This is a biggie for me as I use this trimmer to trim all of the parts of the body that have hair on them.  I have had some of the other trimmers from other manufacturers and they typically come with the adjustable type of guides, or only a few attachments.  I flat out dislike those adjustables for detailed work, and I often forget what setting I need, resulting in having no eyebrows for a week or two *yikes*.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;+ Well made attachments -- All of the guides are made of a durable, yet not \\&quot;plastic-y hard\\&quot; material.  Most of the other manufacturers include those hard plastic guides, which sometimes break (I have broken a few).  The blades all seem well made, they seem to be more precise than the others I have used from other makers.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;+ Soft rubber grip on the handle of the trimmer -- this is fantastic, unlike others I have used, this one does not slip around when using it.  On the downside, it does tend to collect hair on the grip when I am using it.  No big deal, as a quick wipe down/brush off will get it off, and I MUCH prefer the accuracy of not having it slip around in my hand.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Things which I think could be improved:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* I would like to get the rotary attachment with this, for the asking price, or just charge me a little more.  I would like to have it in the box, but I&#x27;m not likely to sit down and actually order that part separately.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* The packaging needs to be updated with the new tray design, and somewhere in the packaging or instructions I would think there should be instructions on how to store the guides and other attachments in the tray holder...  Not a biggie, as with this one I was able to figure it out, but I can see some people not realizing that the front of the trimmer storage area is for storing a blade/shaver head.  The storage is one of the great features, at least in my mind.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* Replaceable battery would be nice -- as my old trimmer wasn&#x27;t what I would refer to as \\&quot;all used up\\&quot;.  I know I could probably send it to a service center since these come with a 5 year warranty, but that&#x27;s not something I&#x27;m likely to do.  I suspect that these use an 18650 Li-ion battery, if that&#x27;s the case I already have some of those.  It would be nice to just pop out the bad one and pop in a replacement vs. buying a whole new trimmer.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* Back to the tray, I think the new design is much, much better (Kudos WAHL!).  It holds everything this time, but for me it would be nice if the tray had the charging adapter built into the bottom of the trimmer holder.  I find it kind of odd to have to guide the wire and plug it in separately.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I really like this trimmer and the attachments that come with it, as can be evidenced by the fact that I bought a second one :)  This is a great trimmer for the \\&quot;semi-pro\\&quot; in you, that wants to have that chiseled look, and control body hair all over.  It&#x27;s a versatile tool that is well thought out and lasts a long time in comparison with some of the other products on the market.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I highly recommend this trimmer!and.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Things which I think could be improved:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;* I would like to get the rotary attachment with this, for the asking price, or just charge me a little more.     <li> I have a short full beard and mustache that I&#x27;ve trimmed with this device for about three months. Based on that experience, I agree with a number of points made in reviews I read here:    CONS    * The packaging is cheap, and there is no carrying or storage case. The plastic packaging materials can be used to hold the various accessories and parts in a primitive tray (which is what&#x27;s pictured), but the plastic molding doesn&#x27;t fit the items particularly well, doesn&#x27;t secure them at all, and is extremely flimsy.  For a product at this price that&#x27;s designed to be used over several years, perhaps while traveling, the absence of a well-designed case costs half a star from my rating.    * It&#x27;s not obvious at a glance -- or indeed, so far as I can tell, possible at all to tell -- when the trimmer is fully charged.  It hasn&#x27;t caught me yet, but some day I&#x27;ll guess wrong and run it out of juice.  (At which point I can see if the quick-charge feature works as billed; I haven&#x27;t tried that yet.)  Minus one quarter-star for lack of an LED charge indicator.    * The documentation is barely adequate. It&#x27;s not intuitively obvious how some of the accessories can be used, or even which of them correspond to the descriptions in tiny print, with bad diagrams, in the multi-lingual instructions. (What help is it for me if there are also Spanish instructions when the English ones are so poor?)  Minus another quarter-star for that.    PROS    * This sucker trims like a demon. It has ample power, and cuts my beard and mustache hairs without snags or pulls.  With very little practice and experimentation, I was achieving perfectly even trims at exactly the lengths I wanted (with different lengths for my beard along my chin and cheeks and for my mustache).    * The plastic beard-length guide looks and feels (as you&#x27;re trying to snap it on) cheesy and insubstantial, but it actually works pretty well.      * Trial and error, plus a bit of patience, will overcome the poor instructions.    * Battery life, while it must be guessed at, is nevertheless quite good.    * The unit is small and light enough that it would be easy and feasible to carry on extended trips (if one had a carrying case).    * I don&#x27;t know if this product would hold up under constant professional use, but it might.  And it seems more than adequately well-made to last for many years of normal consumer use.    CONCLUSION    I always wondered how Patrick Demsey -- Dr. Derek McDreamy on \\&quot;Gray&#x27;s Anatomy\\&quot; -- always manages to keep what looks like a three-day old shadow, without ever being completely clean-shaven or bearded.  One could easily duplicate that look with this tool.  Wahl may not be quite as slick in their marketing as other consumer product companies, but their basic product is a good value.</li>

The blades have always stayed sharp and don&#x27;t pull at all.  Sometimes I will even go a week without shaving, then use the wide blade to trim down my beard so I can shave.  It&#x27;s awesome and really makes shaving so much easier.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I love this product, I&#x27;ve recommended it to all my family and friends, and if it ever dies, I will buy another Wahl.</li>
    <li> I&#x27;ve worn a beard since 1981. I spent years using scissors to keep it under control before buying my first electric trimmer. I&#x27;ve used various Wahl&#x27;s over the years, including corded and cordless types. After the failure of my last one about a year ago I opted for this model. What a difference!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This is easily the best trimmer I&#x27;ve ever used. The nicad&#x27;s slowing gave me warning that it was dying.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I prefer the Wahl narrow head to the wider head of the other manufacturers.     <li> The following is quite long and not quite like a typical review. Skip to the last paragraph for the main points if you&#x27;re not easily entertained.    I bought this trimmer almost 2 years ago now. It worked fine for the first month and then suddenly would not hold a charge. I&#x27;m fairly knowledgeable when it comes to electronics and battery technology and assumed the battery&#x27;s safety mechanism got tripped so it would no longer charge. However, with the trimmer plugged in I could get about a minute of use out of it, which was all I needed for the occasional quick touch-up. I wasn&#x27;t happy, but I dealt with it.    Fast forward to a month ago and, out of nowhere, laziness was suddenly overcome by frustration and outrage. I intentionally bought a half-decent trimmer instead of some $10 piece of throw-away technology; why was I accepting this? Of course, this too was built to be disposable technology, as the battery is clearly not intended to be user-serviceable. But I had a purpose now, and (instead of dealing with some warranty procedure) I took a knife to the cheap rubber shrink-wrapped handle and opened the thing up.    I know I shouldn&#x27;t have expected much, but I was surprised at what I found. At the head of the device is a motor about the size of a quarter. In the handle is a PCB about the size of a stick of gum. It contains the switch mechanism and the electronics necessary to charge the battery. The battery, by the way, is a 3.7V 750mAh Li-ion (14500) and is soldered directly to the PCB. A lot of times when companies make disposable electronics like this, they will at least make the battery easy to remove (once you&#x27;ve destroyed the thing by opening it up) so it can be disposed of properly - not here. At this point I was just tempted to throw it away considering the components cost less the amount I was going to spend on a replacement battery (~$2.50). But I figured it could be a simple project that keeps me from having to spend more money on a replacement or dealing with the warranty (which was probably out now that I had taken it apart).    I picked up a replacement battery from one of those Chinese online retailers (you know, where you might go if you wanted to find a \\&quot;deal\\&quot; that was \\&quot;extreme\\&quot;) and bought a pair of 3.7v 900mAh Li-ions for less than $5 with free shipping. Two weeks later they arrived and I broke out the soldering iron and went to work. The contacts were connected much too securely to the battery, so I melted the solder at the board and just pulled them out. I then took the metal gate off an old 3.5\\&quot; floppy and cut out replacement contacts which I soldered to the new battery. I then punched them back through the trimmer&#x27;s board, touched them up with a little more solder and snapped the case back together. My only regret was cutting off the rubber sheath, which likely would have peeled off in one piece if I had tried that first. I wrapped it up with some electrical tape instead.    Despite the new battery getting pretty hot during some inefficient soldering on my part, it already works at least as good as new. I let the trimmer run for about 10 mins and was satisfied with its performance. The trimmer should have no trouble charging the new battery, as I made sure to splurge on a \\&quot;protected\\&quot; one which should prevent any over-charging or over-draining. Like with the original battery, I&#x27;m going to cycle it completely the first few times to condition the battery. During its first charge it&#x27;s going to sit somewhere fire-resistant just in case.    Tl;dr: What&#x27;s the point? Yeah, this is more of a narrative than a proper review, but there is some good information to be gleaned. Know that this is an extremely cheap piece of electronics. That will be painfully obvious as soon as you pick it up, though it really hits home with a peek inside. Also, realize that it wasn&#x27;t built to last. Sure it&#x27;s got a warranty, and at least someone seems enthusiastic to help based on responses to some of the negative reviews, but who reallywants to hassle with the process? The battery will die in probably 1-3 years, just like the one in your cell phone, you just can&#x27;t replace this one. And, if all you need this for is to trim your sideburns or neck every few weeks, know that you are severely overpaying. You&#x27;re buying this one for its accessories and maybe because it has a Li-ion battery (though that is my, and a few other commenters&#x27;, main complaint). And for those of you who read the whole thing, I don&#x27;t recommend doing what I did, I just shared the steps for entertainment purposes.</li>
    <li> The good: a powerful cutter, great battery. It works, but made me sorely miss my old Norelco Turbo Vacuum Trimmer, so I just gave the Wahl to Goodwill and bought another Norelco Turbo Vac.</li>

I have had clippers that were cheaper but they never trim as well and quickly wear out.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I read many reviews before buying this. I saw comments about it pulling hair. It will pull hair if used incorrectly. There are two ways to hold the trimmer when using. One way is (1) to put the flat side of the clipper head parallel to the skin and the other is (2) to put the flat side of the clipper head perpendicular to the skin. Using method (2) can pull hair and using method (1) has never pulled hair on me.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I would clearly buy this item again and would recommend it to anyone.</li>

I used a damp cloth to wipe it clean, but even the fibers from the cloth somehow got stuck on the handle. The material feels nice when you hold it, but looks messy and is a little annoying to keep clean.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, in terms of its basic function, the trimmer blade works great at trimming neck hair, sideburns, over-ear hair, etc. However, the blades are of questionable quality and mine rusted quickly. This is being marketed as an \\&quot;All-in-One Trimmer\\&quot; and it is not.     <li> This is a great little trimmer.  I already owned a similar trimmer made by Remmington, but this new WAHL trimmer completely trumps the Remington in performance.  When I got it out of the box I was thrilled to see it already had a pretty substantial charge and was ready to go. Immediately I noticed that this trimmer has a ton of torque which I attribute to the Lithium Ion battery. This is very important because if you&#x27;ve ever used a battery powered nose trimmer when the battery is going, you KNOW that when the battery starts to go, hair gets pulled instead of cut. I tried the foil shaver attachment... it actually did a surprisingly decent job and I typically hate foil shavers.  I&#x27;m still not convinced that it will replace my old school manual razor for shaving, but it&#x27;s a good quick option.      Pros:  - Powerful!  - Charges fast and runs long.  - Easy to switch attachments.  - Made in USA. (a rare find these days)  - Built like a tank.    Cons:  - Alot of pieces to keep track of.    - Flimsy organizer tray (but I don&#x27;t use it anyways)  - My old Remington had an adjustable blade guard so you didn&#x27;t have a half dozen pieces laying around.  - Rubber grip attracts hair stubble.          Update:  After using this trimmer for a few months I would have to knock it down a star.  This trimmer is NOT in any way water resistant.  On a couple occasions I would rinse the hair out of the blades and then leave it out to dry.  The trimmer blades will get rust very quickly.  I then went to use the trimmer the other night and it would not turn on.  I proceeded to take it apart and found that the internal circuit board had corrosion across some of the leads to the various chips.  I took an old toothbrush and removed all the corrosion and it began working again.  To ensure this never happened again I coated all the metal contacts with hot glue to keep out the water.  WAHL, what were you thinking?  This thing will set by the sink for it&#x27;s entire life, and you put absolutely no thought into resisting corrosion?  You could have coated the PCB in epoxy, or sealed the internals.  I was able to fix mine, but the average person probably would have just thrown it away.</li>

For example the trimmer and the shaver barley succeed at doing the same job other razors do that are dedicated to the task. It seems they saved the cost of a charging regulator in the trimmer. So in case you lose the wall-brick, don&#x27;t try to replace it with a 5V USB brick, I suppose that you can destroy the battery.&lt;br /&gt;The charger is also 110V only (while most of the countries are using 220V now and a battery powered shaver is likely to be used for travelers...)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In summary: a very nice trimmer showing that Wahl&#x27;s engineering is good and they know how to make good products. But I think that Wahl&#x27;s Marketing is not, and did some wrong choices about cost saving of the charger. I use this every other day before work, it lets me keep a light beard (sporadic since my facial hair hasn&#x27;t decided to fully grow out at the age of 27). It comes with my many attachments, but like other reviewers, i find them cheap and almost pointless.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;THINGS TO KNOW:&lt;br /&gt;this does come with small bottle of blade lube, and i recommend using it. about once a month or 6 weeks i put 1 drop of the lube on the blade and turn on the trimmer so it spreads across all \\&quot;teeth\\&quot;. If you use a drop or 2  every 6 months there is enough to last a few years. i also noticed that the trimmer seemed to get louder as i used it, BUT after lubing it 1 time it brought the noise down and keeps it smooth.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I also use the little comb/brush to brush my hairs out of the trimmer after every use, i think the oils from the hair can wear out the trimmer quicker, which means having it to lube it more frequently.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;the battery last me around 2 weeks, with 3 trims per week. i probably have it on for a bout 3-4 minutes per trim. from sideburns to neck to mustache. i have owned it for at least 6 months with no issues. i only charge it when i can tell it start to slow down, usually over night.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;the bad:&lt;br /&gt;the tray sucks, its way too light and cheap, i couldn&#x27;t even figure out how all the pieces were suppose to fit in it. i like the super rubber grip of the trimmer, but if you pull it from the tray to quick it will just pull the tray with it and all the pieces will go flying everywhere. so i just put all the extra in a zip lock bag and stuck them under the sink. i keep the trimmer and brush/comb in the nearest drawer and your good to go.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I use this all the time, it seems to last a while and i haven&#x27;t had any problems. i wouldnt use it for eyebrows or nose(Norelco NT9110/60 is the bomb for that). If you want something to keep your beard short (not shaven) then this will work, and well. just take care of it, lube and charge accordingly (only when needed). you will be happy with the results.</li>

    <li> [Update on battery life: I wrote this review in May after using the shaver about 15 times without a recharge. Amazingly, I have not recharged the unit since my review and it&#x27;s still going strong! I estimate that I have now enjoyed 30+ shaves without a recharge, with each shave lasting about 3 minutes. The buzzing sound is now a bit erratic, which I interpret as the charge finally wearing off, so I&#x27;m going to plug it in for a recharge.]&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;This review is for the Model 9854L, given to me as a gift. (There are at least 4 different models that look quite similar and may, in fact, be variations of the same basic design. I make no claims about the other similar 3 models.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Bottom Line Up Front: This is a very capable beard trimmer with a very long battery life. It&#x27;s comfortable to hold and has many attachments. Recommended.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My usage pattern is to trim my beard about every 4 days. I keep it at a 2-week length, well above \\&quot;stubble\\&quot; length but still quite short (less than  inch). (People have called it a \\&quot;banker&#x27;s beard\\&quot;.) I don&#x27;t style it or do anything special - just zoom the trimmer along the grain of my beard using the #2 length guide, then work the trimmer against the grain to cut my mustache. I always use the full-size cutting head rather than bothering to swap it out for the  inch trimmer head.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The trimmer is comfortably light, with just enough heft to feel solid but not enough to tire my hand. The rubberized handle is exceedingly sticky, making for a secure grip. There are 3 snap-on short-hair trimming guides - 5 lengths would have been better to cover all possibilities, but I make do with the #2 guide.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;There are several trimming heads that easily swap out. I always use the basic \\&quot;full\\&quot; trimming head, but there&#x27;s a  inch fine trimmer (without any trimming guides, just the bare razor head) and another head for deburring neck hair. The different heads snap off and on easily as long as you remember to remove the trimming guides first.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The retail package has the usual number of cheap combs and brushes. Nothing to write home about, but they do the job. And there&#x27;s a stand on which you can mount all the components. Since I only use the trimmer, I just put everything in a drawer and forget about the stand.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The lithium-ion battery life is astounding for a unit like this. I&#x27;m used to getting only 4 to 5 trims per charge from a typical battery operated beard trimmer. With this Wahl 9854L, I&#x27;m getting over 15 trims per charge and I&#x27;ve not yet let the battery run all the way down.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;What&#x27;s not to like? As some others have mentioned, the rubberized handle is so sticky that facial hair clings tenaciously to it when you brush it or wipe it with a cloth. At first this bothered me a lot, even though I appreciated the safety value of the sticky handle. However, I discovered that the hairs come off quickly when I blow on them, so this is no longer an issue for me. [Update after 6 months of use: The stickyness wears off, leaving a very comfortable, non-slip grip. Still need to blow on the unit to get rid of the hairs, but it&#x27;s not nearly as much of an issue as when it was new.]&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The razor makes quite a buzzing sound. Don&#x27;t get me wrong, you don&#x27;t need to wear ear protection when you use it, but the sound can be heard (albeit faintly) through a closed bathroom door.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The power supply is small and light, but it&#x27;s only 120V - a problem for me because I live in a dual-voltage house. If you decide to take this puppy on an overseas trip lasting less than a couple of months, just charge the trimmer and leave the power supply at home to prevent blowing it up when plugging it into a 220V outlet... or am I the only one who&#x27;s ever done that?</li>

    <li> The Wahl Lithium Ion All In One Grooming Kit is a great product with adequate instructions. As a result, once I called the company and figured out how to use everything that came with the product I was very happy.    I like this product because it comes with four easily changeable \\&quot;blades\\&quot; that can be attached to the base. The blades include a trim blade to use on beards and mustaches, a precision detailer to use on nose and ear hair as well as eyebrows, a dual shaver to use on faces if they do not have a beard and finally a clipper blade to use on the hair on one&#x27;s head. All of the the blades work well. I also read in the instructions any of these blades can be used on other parts of one&#x27;s body that are shaved or need to be shaved.        This product also comes with seven guide combs that easily attach to the trimmer and can be used to help with grooming. Also included is a brush for cleaning the blades, a small comb, and some blade oil. All of these fit nicely into a stand.    Finally, this product comes with a lithium ion rechargeable battery that charges in a shorter amount of time in comparison to regular batteries and keeps a charge longer as well. It also comes with a 5 year limited warranty.     I am impressed with the number of uses for the grooming kit and like the idea of a lithium ion battery. Once charged up it does hold its charge well and is easy to recharge.     All of the blades work well but I am still trying to figure out how the guide combs work. The reason I am still figuring out about the guide combs is because of the instructions.     The instructions are on one piece of paper. The paper is folded in half and then has seven folds. In effect you have 14 squares that are 2 inches by 4 inches. The top half of the instructions tell about the warranty, things to do to keep safe, how to charge the battery and how to care for the trimmer. Since the instructions are the same for three different models one panel lists the other two models.    The lastseven panels talk about the product. The type is smaller that that used on the safety instructions on the top panel and I found it a chore to read.    One problem is since these instructions are for three models I could not figure out why my trimmer did not have a rotating head like it said in the instructions until I realized that the instructions were referencing a different model.       There are some drawings that are somewhat helpful but they are small. I used the back of the box to figure out how some things work. I also called the company to figure out a couple of things.  Had the instructions used larger type and diagrams like the back of the box I would have had an easier time understanding how everything worked.      While the instructions are a bit of a problem they can&#x27;t take away from how well this product works. The grooming kit is truly all in one and has many uses. I like the lithium ion battery. Ultimately, I am extremely pleased with the grooming kit and I recommend it.</li>

Well, I&#x27;ve been using it every other day for a week and a half since and it hasn&#x27;t died yet. So, I&#x27;m pretty pleased with the overall battery life. But, this brings me to my first issue. It has no light or anything to tell you when it&#x27;s fully charged. All I ask for is a little LED or something that lights up or blinks when charged. But, no such luck with this trimmer.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;My other relatively minor issue is the tray for the attachments. I have no idea how they fit everything in the tray. I don&#x27;t even have the haircut attachments in there, since I&#x27;m not ever using those, and I still can&#x27;t fit everything in it nicely. It&#x27;s just a small, cheap, plastic tray that doesn&#x27;t serve much purchase.     <li> OK, I&#x27;ve used lots of hair cutters and have learned that there are somethings to be careful to look for:&lt;br /&gt;1.  Short cords - This doesn&#x27;t have a cord at all, and the battery life is long, so it&#x27;s a winner.&lt;br /&gt;2.  Stamped steel blades - Stamped steel blades don&#x27;t last and they pull hair.  These are machined; &#x27;nother winner.&lt;br /&gt;3.  Noisy clippers don&#x27;t last.  Think about it; that noise, that hammering sound that you hear is something... hammering. The little clipper is beating itself to death somehow, and eventually, probably pretty soon, it will quit.  This one is quiet for the win.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The \\&quot;organizer\\&quot; that this set comes with is pretty useless, but only because it doesn&#x27;t weigh anything.  I turned mine over, filled it with BB shot (fishing aisle, Wal-Mart, $1.29) and topped it all off with Shoe Goo (also at Wal-Mart).  Now the stand has a nice weight, and stays where I put it.  I also got rid of the shaver attachment and the guards that I won&#x27;t use (there really isn&#x27;t room for EVERYTHING, so you have to choose what you will use).  Now everything fits nice and neat.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I&#x27;ve had this for about four months now, and it&#x27;s the best all-rounder that I have come across.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Update:  I&#x27;ve been using this clipper once a week for a year, and it still looks and performs as new. After the first year, I started observing that the charge will not hold for more than a few minutes, steadily decreasing. For the last three months, the trimmer charge lasts under a minute after a full day of charging. Other review have described rusting and poor quality rubber grip, I agree.  This is light trim, no heavy duty stuff here..&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Of course batteries degrade and die, some earlier than others. I took the trimmer to the repair shop indicated on the Walh website. Guess what, I found that this $45 trimmer is a throwaway item. I was quoted $40 llabor + cost of a new battery. The tech said the battery is not swappable, it is \\&quot;hard wired\\&quot;/soldered on.</li>
    <li> An excellent trimmer, as far as how it cuts. BUT - this is a throw away piece, one in which Wahl did not intend the user to ever be able to change the battery! They seem to expect one to simply throw it away when the battery goes bad and buy another  trimmer from them!! But, if you&#x27;re a technically oriented person, the battery is available from Amazon:     http://www.amazon.com/Cylindrical-Rechargeable-Batteries-Philips-Electric/dp/B00ML5K2OG/ref&#x3D;sr_1_1?s&#x3D;electronics&amp;ie&#x3D;UTF8&amp;qid&#x3D;1422152997&amp;sr&#x3D;1-1&amp;keywords&#x3D;3.7+volt+aa+battery+with+solder+tabs%27    Or, search the web for, 3.7 Volt Li-Ion battery, size 14500 (or AA) with solder tabs. It&#x27;s available from most all battery dealers. The rubber skin covering the plastic case can be pealed back from the head to the tail, to remove it. Doing so will turn it inside out. When the work is done, it can be turned back right side out and pulled back over the body into place with a bit of effort. But, if you don&#x27;t care about having a rubber grip, you might as well simply slice it off with a razor blade &amp; forget about reusing it - your choice. Then, the case is easily pried open, using a small screwdriver. One will need circuit board repair &amp; soldering skills to un-solder the old battery from the circuit board &amp; to install the replacement battery, and minimal mechanical skills in order to reassemble the unit. If you&#x27;re willing to do all of this, then it&#x27;s a great trimmer! The only other issue I&#x27;ve had with it is the small trimming head began to work a bit intermittently, so I ordered a replacement from Wahl with no difficulties and at a reasonable price. However, Wahl has revealed itself to be a very consumer &amp; environmentally unfriendly company with this design, as most folks will simply send a good piece of machinery, &amp; a used up Li-Ion battery along with it, to their local landfill, simply because it needs a new battery!! I openly gave it 5 stars in hopes that more folks will see the review, but it really only deserves 2 or 3!</li>

    <li> I&#x27;ve had quite a few trimmers over the years.  I have a sensitive face, and don&#x27;t like to shave every day, so between shaves I trim the stubble.  All my past trimmers had several problems.  They would occasionally pull hair instead of cutting it, the batteries wouldn&#x27;t hold a charge very long, the charge they would hold would diminish over time, and the motors seemed to lose some power.  Also, recommended charge time was typically 12 - 15 hours.  Of course that&#x27;s because all my old trimmers had NiMH batteries.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Then I got the Wahl in December of 2011.  It&#x27;s lightweight, but you can really feel the power the first time you shave.  No pulling hair, just a nice, clean cut.  The first time you charge, they recommend charging for 1 hour.  This thing holds a charge great, too.  The Lithium Ion batteries are so much better!  I see more trimmers offer the Lithium batteries than they did a year ago, but not many in this price range.  I can&#x27;t say just how long the batteries last, but they seem to go on forever.  I keep thinking it must be ready to die soon, but it just keeps going.  So it&#x27;s easy to charge before it dies.  Forget about &#x27;battery memory&#x27; with Lithium, there isn&#x27;t any.  Any charge will do.  You don&#x27;t want to charge or discharge them too much, but Lithium batteries generally have built in safeguards against that happening.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;There are a few cons, but nothing worth taking off a star.  Other trimmers offer &amp;#34;lube for life&amp;#34;, meaning you never have to oil the blades.  You do need to oil the blades on this Wahl.  However, it&#x27;s pretty easy to put a drop or 2 of oil on the blades once a week, and it helps give a smooth shave.  I have a feeling the the oil free trimmers might be more for planned obsolescence.  Lubed for life, just a short life.  The storage &#x27;rack&#x27; is pretty cheap, and the pieces don&#x27;t fit all that great.  If you use it, don&#x27;t bump it.  I just keep my trimmer and accessories in a drawer cubby.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I would definitely recommend this trimmer.  If you need different features, at least try to find a lithium or a trimmer that also works off AC while plugged in.</li>

I like the lithium battery but am highly disappointed in having the trimmmer go on the fritz so soon after I purchased it. How can something with a 5 year warranty last only one month and a half? Had it not been for it suddenly becoming unusable I would have given this product 5 stars. One star is too high for a product only lasting one and a half months.    Update on Jan 8, 2015. I finally figured what went wrong. The clipper insert broke. There is a metal piece (spring) on the back side of the clipper attachment which broke. I didn&#x27;t have to unscrew the phillips head screws, I just needed to pull off the whole head. I noticed a metal piece on the bathroom counter, and it was from the attachment. I ordered the part from www.wahl-store.com and inserted it into the handle (the battery operated thing) and the clippers work great now. The part I ordered is WAH 59300-800. It&#x27;s listed in the written material as part # 59300. I&#x27;m still upset that this clipper head broke after only 6 weeks, however the fix was relatively inexpensive. The part I ordered cost $7.50 plus $5.95 postage and handling. I ordered two and my total bill was $20.95. I&#x27;m not changing my rating since I have purchased a different brand clipper in the mean time. I just thought it appropriate to update my review. So, If the clipper ever sounds like a mini chain saw and doesn&#x27;t clip well at all, it just might be the blade portion and a fix is relatively easy.</li>
